<div id="review_1455952285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455952285" />
    <a title="Genevieve Chao" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47077179-genevieve-chao"><img alt="Genevieve Chao" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455952285?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Genevieve Chao" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Genevieve Chao" href="/user/show/47077179-genevieve-chao">Genevieve Chao</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455952285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11979063360362545189">The novel, “Tiger Eyes” by Judy Blume is a great book about how deal with something tragic and move on.I chose this book because I read the back and it sounded like a good story. <br/> Davey, a high school girl from Atlantic City, New Jersey has just lost her father because he was shot when managing his store. Her mom, her brother, and her move temporarily to New Mexico to live with her aunt and uncle. One day Davey goes to a canyon to get her mind off things. While in the canyon she meets a boy name</span>
  <span id="freeText11979063360362545189" style="display:none">The novel, “Tiger Eyes” by Judy Blume is a great book about how deal with something tragic and move on.I chose this book because I read the back and it sounded like a good story. <br /> Davey, a high school girl from Atlantic City, New Jersey has just lost her father because he was shot when managing his store. Her mom, her brother, and her move temporarily to New Mexico to live with her aunt and uncle. One day Davey goes to a canyon to get her mind off things. While in the canyon she meets a boy named Wolf. She tells him her name is Tiger and they meet in the canyon regularly. She soon goes back to school and meets and new friend named Jane. Her and Jane go to the hospital to volunteer during the week. She finds a bond with a dying man named Mr. Ortiz. Little does she know that is Wolf's father. Mr. Ortiz soon dies and her mom announces they will move back to New Jersey and get a new start. While she is sad to leave everything in New Mexico she is ready to go back home.<br /> The ending in this book wraps up very nicely. Davey says goodbye to all her friends and leaves things for Wolf to remember her by in the canyon. She leaves excited to see them again one day and happy to go back home. My favorite part in this book was when Davey finds out Mr Ortiz is Wolf’s dad. I liked this part because she finds a new connection with Wolf. <br /> I really enjoyed this book. It has symbolism and a good plot. If you like books the are realistic fiction you should read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11979063360362545189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('weHJflPcniIlRcPMDrdFs6fqqlRKOzZuEokQAKDHdmgEElFU30VOR5fEEnY5XbUiPPezAwj1yQOJDBb5JuD9KA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

The story revolves arou<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8232590543349951671\" style=\"display:none\">Humsafar is a romantic novel written by Farhat Ishtiaq. The novel was first published in 7 parts in Khawateen Digest monthly from July 2007 to January 2008. It was later published as a complete novel by Ilm-o-Irfan Publishers. The story revolves around Ashar and Khirad\'s relationship with their daughter, Hareem, and how she unknowingly bridges the distances that exist between her parents. The novel is written in a retrospective manner and told mostly in flashbacks. The first half of the novel is based on mostly Ashar’s reflections and his point of view while the second part of the novel is told mainly from Khirad’s point of view.\n\nThe story has been adapted into a drama serial (Humsafar), produced by Momina Duraid and directed by Sarmad Sultan Khoosat.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12942.Judy_Blume">About Judy Blume</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12942.Judy_Blume"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1430843076p3/12942.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/12942.Judy_Blume">Judy Blume
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
8,718
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3562490455410435061">Judy Blume spent her childhood in Elizabeth, New Jersey, making up stories inside her head. She has spent her adult years in many places doing the same thing, only now she writes her stories down on paper. Adults as well as children will recognize such Blume titles as: Are You There God? It's Me, Margaret; Blubber; Just as Long as We're Together; and the five book series about the irrepressible Fu</span>
  <span id="freeText3562490455410435061" style="display:none">Judy Blume spent her childhood in Elizabeth, New Jersey, making up stories inside her head. She has spent her adult years in many places doing the same thing, only now she writes her stories down on paper. Adults as well as children will recognize such Blume titles as: Are You There God? It's Me, Margaret; Blubber; Just as Long as We're Together; and the five book series about the irrepressible Fudge. She has also written three novels for adults, Summer Sisters; Smart Women; and Wifey, all of them New York Times bestsellers. More than 80 million copies of her books have been sold, and her work has been translated into thirty-one languages. She receives thousands of letters a year from readers of all ages who share their feelings and concerns with her.<br />Judy received a B.S. in education from New York University in 1961, which named her a Distinguished Alumna in 1996, the same year the American Library Association honored her with the Margaret A. Edwards Award for Lifetime Achievement. Other recognitions include the Library of Congress Living Legends Award and the 2004 National Book Foundation's Medal for Distinguished Contribution to American Letters.<br />She is the founder and trustee of The Kids Fund, a charitable and educational foundation. She serves on the boards of the Author's Guild; the Society of Children's Book Writers and Illustrators; the Key West Literary Seminar; and the National Coalition Against Censorship.<br />Judy is a longtime advocate of intellectual freedom. Finding herself at the center of an organized book banning campaign in the 1980's she began to reach out to other writers, as well as teachers and librarians, who were under fire. Since then, she has worked tirelessly with the National Coalition Against Censorship to protect the freedom to read. She is the editor of Places I Never Meant To Be, Original Stories by Censored Writers.<br />Judy has completed a series of four chapter books -- The Pain &amp; the Great One -- illustrated by New Yorker cartoonist James Stevenson. She has co-written and produced a film adaptation of her book Tiger Eyes, and is currently writing a new novel.<br />Judy and her husband George Cooper live on islands up and down the east coast. They have three grown children and one grandchild.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3562490455410435061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
